Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be a clavele, which we have previously shown; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been previously written.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the inflammation of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and are full of bitter yellow fluid, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and anular; and lift your hand with the cauter without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not insert it too deeply, lest the bitter yellow fluid should flow out, and let the cauter be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After doing so, make two cauterizations on each leg at the point of the cutellaire; and let the cauterization be from top to bottom, one above the knee in front and the other behind, within the leg; and leave the cauterizations uncovered for a long time without curing, so that the water exits; after curing with other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the swelling
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are afflicted, and cannot be cured by methods of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with strong virtue, if you do. Then make a great cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken before or cautery of the stomach, to the circular cautery; and three cauteries around the subtle bowel to each subtle cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the finger, and one cautery on each eyelid, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is profitable when it has good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, one or more, and are old and of gross cold and moist corrupted humors, and are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit if you make cauterizations: III on the spine of the back, which is all deflected downwards a little and a little in triangles, and I cauterize downwards the belly II fingers; and if you think that the stomach is refrigerated, and the food does not cook, and one sees the face inflating, then make a great cauterization on the stomach, as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the clave cauterizations; and let the cauterization stay overt for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the limb so that it may be healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the skin condition named "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cope with thelul, if you heat the cautery that seems to be a rasp, and then place it all ablaze on the affected thelul area; and leave it until your hand feels the cauteries reaching the origin of the vein, from which the blood flows out; do this once or twice, and if there is much of thelul, then cautery each spot as we have said; after the treatment of beneficial ointments, they will be healthy again; and if you cautery with a large cautery on the affected area, it will provide greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot suffer tailoring or surgery, which we will recount in its place, if a disease comes that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes, and it is wrapped and cast in putrid and corrupt moisture, if you need to prove all of a subtle probe, and take care that you know the entire extent of how deep it has penetrated.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery that seems to be a rasp, and putting it in the fistula according to the quantity that the probe has entered, and recommencing the cautery as long as the putrid and corrupt flesh are burnt, one time, or two, or three, according to the quantity of their need; and beware of touching the nerve that is nearby, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and intestines, beware of these parts, and do not make false passages in the flesh, and think that it is not personally affected; after healing the limb so that it may be healthy, and if the limbs are healed, and the materials are removed a long time, then know that the limbs are entirely healthy; and if the materials are not removed, know that the limbs are troubled, and corrupt the bone at the foundation; and thus one of these things that we will say about his limb.
de la maladie des reins	of the kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the loins, and of great windiness, and does not take hold of a woman, then it is necessary that you apply cautery on both sides of the loins at the cautery claw which we mentioned before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in line, and they will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is numb and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then you must apply cautery on the upper part above the bladder, where the hairs begin to grow, and one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery as long as we need for a poultice; and make three cauteries above the back, or two if you have no need of them; and let the claw-shaped cautery be according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends delayed; and when they come, it feels great pain: then one must apply three cauteries around the belly, just as we said about the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries below the back; and let the cauteries be gentle, just as we said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist vapors descend to the hip bone, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the places of the division are visible, then one must apply a cautery to the patient on the hip bone with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark beforehand the place around the hip as it turns, so that the hip is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you are not present for these cauteries, make three cauteries of the olive branch, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the wounds; and heal until they are healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the ankle
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the ankle joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is not cured by what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of doing cautery is in two ways: it is to know combining medicines burning, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many ways, of which one is such: that you cauterize on the surface of the thigh three triangular cauteries in this form, and make good depth and width, and leave between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be oval; sometimes one does not make cautery in the middle on top of the thigh, because there are four according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if you cauterize with a circle of fire that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the thigh; but do it in such a way that the circles encompass the entire thigh, and all the spaces of the skin are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And it is the manner in which one does on the thigh, when the pain holds in the thigh, and does not reach just to the knee nor just to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches to the knee and leg, make two cauteries there where the patient says the pain holds, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers, a little to the left side; and let the cauteries be cellular, and let the thickness of the burn be moderate; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes or near the ankle, cauterize where they feel the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the mastery is, make more of it; and if it is known that the pain is beneath the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery at the cutellaire or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave so much of the cautery that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause more nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have undergone cauterization on the shin of the foot, and they let it be until the leg was completely swollen, and the feet also, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout the feet.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a burst of belly which he got death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, perform cauterization on one and the other, in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said about the cauterization of the thigh, that this is the method: make such an iron rod as thick as a little finger, or a little less, and it should be between two irons, and it should be like a nutmeg, and there are two irons, and they should also be like a claw, and it has a well-made handle of iron; and this is the form.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is totally red hot and gives off sparks, and then place it on the diseased hainch's boil, and turn it towards the healthy side; and cauterize once with a round cautery and leave it for three days; and then apply a poultice of butter, and let the wound stay open for a long time; after the treatment of ointment until it is fully healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its effect, and we see few who use it; and however, this is one of the good cauteries, which can alleviate suffering, and there where it is effective.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The fire cauterizers are such that you make the instrument between the fingers in the margin of the gate, and be it of iron or a long arrow, and in the height have II among us, and among each one the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and be open below and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing on the box of the hip of the patient lying on his good side, and after putting your hand much on the box of the hip; then insert between the II circles of the warm water which is warmed by fire I poke, and let it for an hour and a half, and suffer the patient to have heat and dryness.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is true that he finds moderation as from fire; and when the moderations are past, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hip of warm water, and let thus III days, and put on a poultice so long as what is black from the wound is opened; and leave III days that the putrefaction is straightened; and this would be the last aid after the cure of ointments so that he may be healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make the instrument that you hold according to what you have done in the same way; and this is the method of warm poultice, and I have written about treating with medicine for rectification.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take equal parts of alkaline and living chalk, as much of one as of the other, and crush them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Where it has a small hole for the point of a razor to enter; and put on top of that pot another well-plugged pot, and put above the alkaline and chalk and sweet dew above, until there is a duo of powders as you have well prepared with your hand; and let it sit thus until it descends into the watery and clear pot, then take all that dew, and pour it on the chalk and on the alkaline as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And when it will be very sharp and is administered in many medical procedures and in cauteries of other members, because it performs another work like fires, and if there are other medicines that one cauterizes well the hainche thus as thesis and honey and anacardi and chalk with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galien tells us about a cure where a man was cured of the pain of the hainche and sciatic vein, and the doctor said that there is no other cure, and he was healed at once when they did this cure, and he was bathed as it is described hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this manner that you should take fresh and dry litargire, and crush it much with a little fat, and apply it to the hainche and thigh and leg where the pain is, and bind; and let it be for three hours, and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the bitterness.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a warm bath so that his body is somewhat relaxed, and make him enter into bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healthy.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And beware that no one should use fire cautery with such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with fiery iron, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be performed in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and the old oil of a elder tree, and apply it to the hollow which is between the thumb of the foot and the other called the "fossil".
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take dry iron of a dry tree, and heat it in the fire until it is charcoal, and apply it to the linen, and let it stay until it is warm; and do it again thus, and do not cease from doing thus until you think by sensation that it reaches the ham, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of a dry tree".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by fall or percussion or by too great an evacuation, or by similar signs of cold expanded matter, none of these signs is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is fitting after this that the patient is emptied of filthy pills or other similar things, that one makes on their back, there where the pain holds, three marked lines of an inch, and in each line 5 or more cauterizations according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; and let the cauterization be made according to the cauterizer called "poins"; and if you see, make 3 or 4 cauterizations at the cauterizer claw-like middle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a contracted limb when they lift themselves up, and fear; and you find in the upper part of the spine of the back and in the appearance that comes upon the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, if you cauterize at the cautery of that according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery penetrates deeply into each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that, if you cauterize around the spine with a piercing fire cautery at two or three lines, and be the points close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After healing the limb so that it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply fire cautery in a curved manner which is in a spasm of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of the joints is from moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes on foot, which they properly call "podagra", and when it is from cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make a mound of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-like according to this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the surface of the foot, make the fire cautery at the entire fire cautery which one calls a "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come near the knees and other joints, and this happens often, make the fire cautery on each knee three or four times, at the entire olive-fire cautery; and if you have need of more, do more, but do not hold your hand too long, only as long as the space of the heart is warm.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and back, one administers the cautery that we mentioned in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the finger II lines; and if there remains a point of pain in the two, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come just to the wrists or just to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good governance for the patient and prepare medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good governance and you purge evil humors, it will be healthy with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the treatment of this face
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes from anger, and the belly descends to the hips and it is newly formed, then you must ensure that when you want to cure it, it does not harm anyone on that day; and that it uses things that ease the belly, so that the filth descends from its belly; afterwards, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his flanks as long as the belly is being repaired, and reset them with your fingers, and sign underneath the rupture on the bone of the thumb, and at all a sign that resembles half a circle above the body; then apply the cautery in the form that it is.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is clear and it casts a healthy scent.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the boules to their place; and the minister holds his hand so they do not return again; and work well on the hips of the patient, and put under him one cushion and one strap on the hips, and another on the foot which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign of the whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, so recommence again until you come to the bone; and be subtly wary that the boule does not slip when you make the cautery; lest you burn it; and lest by this the patient may die or have another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your operations are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to the measure of their bones, and for large people also large according to their measure; after three days cure the limb with a warm cautery so that the stiffness is removed; after curing other wounds so that they are healthy, and let the patient lie 40 days on his back so that the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that their bandages be loosened gradually, so that the boil does not burst when they get up to go to their chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when they want to get up, a well-made splint is applied to them, and for another 40 days; and let them have good rest, so that they work little and beware of too great repletion from drinking and eating, and from too high spirits; and when they follow this teaching, they will be entirely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will tell you afterwards about the treatment of a wound in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the route of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds come to other parts and are acquainted, and you see that they do not grow anymore, have the fire cautery made of double fire according to its quantity, and be prepared for the third day of the treatment; afterwards, treat according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize at the angle of the fire in three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the level of the notch and make a line for the width above the wound, and another below, and hold your hand in all the cauterized places.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more gentle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in no member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to a member, whether from a fall or a blow, and that pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine is of no value, then it is necessary for it to be cauterized with the cautery called "points", and let the cauterizations be according to the length of the member and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twisting and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is sufficiently healthy for the first cautery, that's good; if not, begin another cautery on top of that one, because such is the custom that it should be moved to the adjacent member, since it is necessary that you do the cauteries until the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	of sickness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The limbs are often helped many times by cautery with great assistance, and especially the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can't you see that cautery should be applied where the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the entire disease, then you make five cauteries on the head: I behind the ear, and another towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; and II at the II horns, and I at the back on the hairline; and you leave it so long as your hand until the cauteries come just to the bone, and until the scabs issue forth, so that the vapors of the gross humors can issue forth; and you cautery on the mouse according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is scattered throughout; and it appears manifestly, then it is necessary that you make cauteries of these cauteries that we have said on the head, and .i. cautery in the soft part of the nose, and .ij. cauteries on the spine of the neck, and .vj. cauteries on the spine of the back, and .i. great on the chest and .i. another on the ribs, and .ij. on the shoulders; and .ij. on the hips, and .ij. on the tendons of the foot, and .i. on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the rear calcifying, so you do not burn them; and many times make a cautery on the bone of the finger, and .i. another on the bone of the stomach, and .i. another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you do of cauterization, the more you do of aid, and it benefits him; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from cauterization if the healthy person feels it, because the body is already totally corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in ways of fires.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After healing the wound with flour of various times with honey and other treatments until it be sound.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation comes to a member and is treated with medicines and ointments and emplasters, and it is not sound, then you make cauterizations on the member according to its size and the smallness of the member; and let the cautery be a little inside the skin of the heart; then treat with unctions until it be sound.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And often one performs cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the outlet of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus if it is swollen; and in no way should one interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and outlets of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of abscesses
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "abscesses" is inflamed, and the engines of medicine are of no value, then cauterize with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the skin of the heart, until the whiteness is removed, and its color changes; then cure with flour of veal and lentils with oil of rose and leaves of plantain, and blood of colon and blood of almond, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a dressing, and apply it to the wound until it is healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of cancer by cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre (cancer or ulcer) appears at the beginning, and you want to stop it, if you cauterize with the cautery that seems to circle around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And wise men say that one should perform cautery also in the middle of the chancre; and it does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already wanted to avoid it; and a more correct thing is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circule", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the inflammation that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have a disease called "adubelati", and it delays healing because of the superfluity which it causes or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you see hasten to heal: then cauterize extensively with many small cauteries in pricking; afterwards let them be.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it hastens to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you perceive the fire cautery to be entirely burnt, heat the cautery of wood that is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" so that the cauteries penetrate to the heart, and be such the cauteries that the patient feels them piercing in some manner that the course of the purulence is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment so that it may be perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease there is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a withering of members, for it withers the members just as the fire dries up the dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in someone who can suffer from cautery along with fire, then heat the small and large cauteries gently according to what is suitable for the person or the disease; after cauterizing all parts so that you eradicate all corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and apply the cauterized areas with a warm poultice made with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of swollen limbs generates scar.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy skin does not grow, it's good; and if not, then resume the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this method has often been cured by medical treatment along with fire cautery; but nevertheless fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the treatment of medical treatment in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the pores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that the feet are affected by a disease called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large swollen thing which blisters the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are in two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat the cautery iron as if it were a pen of vaulted fire, and make it from good iron to the measure that it can pierce the nail from all parts, and that it has subtle edges; afterwards, you put it totally hot on the nail, and turn your hand entirely around the nail until it comes to the font of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to rot and decay; then make a plaster of malve savages, boiled with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be disrooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound of inflammation by burning so long as it becomes healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by evil humors of the body, and many times it happens in hands and feet, then you must apply warm cautery; and it is in this manner: take a cane of iron or a piece of heated wood, and place it on the nail and the heel, that is to say for removing warts; and place the cane so that it surrounds everything around, then put a little hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and then find the warm water deep into the root; and let the patient suffer a little the burning of the warm water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will uproot everything to its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, as you stretch those who are in the body, then heal the wounds that cause shame.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people shiver with cold or nerves, or from quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you apply three fire cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one fire cauterization between each vertebra; and one fire cauterization or foot, and one on the stomach for olive fire cauterization; if they stop shivering, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled pimples
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never appear by default on the body's surface, or pus-filled boils, which come from gross corrupt matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	it is necessary first when they appear that one makes cauterization on each head of the boil: a subtle cauterization of fir of myrtle, whose tip is seized by fire, or of root of aristology long, or of lentricular cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from the evil humors beforehand, but are dislodged the superfluities from which they come, and are healthy; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Here is the translation:
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it so much that the blood is pacified beneath your finger, and does not issue more; then apply fire cautery, small and large as much as they are all red; then take into account, whether great or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is located, and apply the cautery on this vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery so that the blood is restored.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it happens to be when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take quickly another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood is stanched; and beware that you do not harm the nerve that is nearby, and that another evil does not come upon the patient; and know that when blood flows out of the artery, it cannot be well stanched unless the artery is large, so it is not by one of the three ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with a thread, or by medicines applied that have the power to stanch blood; and thus it will be tied and held in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers the stanching of the blood closely with cloth or puts things tightly on, or similar things, it will not be of much use.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to no one and there is no better medicine present, then you must put your finger index on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well so that it rests above the wound and above the vein; and do not move your finger, but let the cold froide moisture penetrate so that the blood is congealed and thickened and rested; and make an inquiry beforehand about what he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book on surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have said in the first chapter all about the disease where it is necessary to use fire cautery, or burning medicine, and the tools and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I placed that chapter at the head just below the feet, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same method because one finds it easier to follow what one desires.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one of the cauteries, and therefore it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you that you do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come of those who harm themselves with their illness so that they die easily from the frenzy that they find in their disease, and from the greatness of their evil; and of these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there is one who gives his opinion, and says: "wait, I am cured"; and the disease is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but place greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not open foolishly but wisely of those things of which you are certain, and of which you can have taken and lost; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of long duration.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Fathers give you good understanding and direction, and if you want to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Here is the translation:
dou chief plein d’aigue	Here is the translation:
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Here is the translation:
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this disease except in children, and of those that I have seen, death hastens them; and therefore it seems to me that it is worth leaving the work on certain treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head swelled every day so much that he could not hold it up; and the moisture was so great that it became mortified, and this moisture is assembled beneath the bone under the siphac, between the heart and the bone; and the treatments are such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you make a large incision in the head; and let it be as long as our, until the moisture runs; and see there the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more increased, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the signs that you observe the commissures of the head overcome by each part, and the water flows out when you press with your hand inside, and it does not respond to you: then it is necessary that you make three incisions in the head according to this method:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all moisture thoroughly.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding together the edges of bandages and powders, and apply wine and oil, and let it be so until the fifth day; then disengage, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head be aligned properly, and give the patient dry food free from moisture as much as possible until the limb is comforted and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look to open the greatness of the abscess, and assemble the water; for it is never in front; never behind; never on the right; and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the abscess opens, and fill with water, and do it according to what you have the power; and beware that you do not cut an artery; and let flow blood, so that the patient may die from the corruption of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of swelling
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or at the foot, and the disease is chronic, and the medical treatment does not benefit, then the last resort is cauterization with fire, which one will cover the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, when you have seen the wounds close, that the patient makes their head rear; after rubbing the place of a rough bandage until the arteries appear, then reset the patient's neck with all the bandages; then look where the vein beats, and the veins on one side and the other are behind the ears, and a little are responded to; then sign the veins of the wound, then cover one and the other with a sharp pointed instrument of two edges, until the vein is reached near the bone, and that should be through the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the pointed instrument beneath the artery and cover above, cutting thus as .ij. two fingers in width.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is covered, then the blood flows back continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feeling, then you must measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign from the notch and make just to the bone; and it is necessary to put six drops of blood, or by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if there remains on the bone point of the syphac, then cover that abscesses do not come, then hold the wound and bind it, and the treatment of ointment until it is healthy.
de emigrainne	of the migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient migration comes, and catarrh arrives, due to the moisture of the tears and the warmth in the temples, and the old worn-out forehead and similar things, and it is treated by methods of cures of medicine and all that does not profit him, if we extract the arteries from the temples and the cauterizations, as we have related.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes the hairs of their temples fall, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is little restored unless in some homes which are too cold; and if it is restored, then extract from the neck of the patient some drapels, then scrub the skin with some rough cloth, and raise the skin with warm water so that the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula made in this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then lift it up with pincers, and separate well the tissues that are beneath each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it to the point of the unguina, then cover that part according to the quantity of two inches.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Because she is not bandaged, if she does not feel the wound entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	Here is the translation:
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cautery is aid to finish the swellings: because it is of great aid against swellings.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries that one fills the old cotton with a lot of cotton and places well-made tents; and when they are removed, if they are treated with dry medicines that make flesh grow, and with tents, until it is healthy; and if without cutting the artery so much as you observe, if you hasten to cover with cautery, or you fill the old cotton with vitriol and hold it in your hand so the blood is stopped; and if you do not have this present, place your finger on the spot until the blood is congealed, and raise the cold water spot so the blood ceases, and be steady as necessary; and what is more gentle and easier in extracting the artery is that you cautery the vein of this trenchant cautery, but the trenchant should be well spaced to avoid longer delay.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold less their warmth.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And you should have between the .ij. knives .i. a thickness of a finger, and then when you have signed to engrave the .ij. veins, and you place the hot iron on them so much that it reaches just up to the bone, and covers the vein in .ij. veins; and they should be spaced between the .ij. joints because it is not necessary to cauterize all of this cautery throughout; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are overflowing from veins that are on the top of the head, and it does not profit from any medicine that one makes, and you see the face of the patient become red, and feel an uneven walk as if of a tremor; and since they are tense and moist so that the hairs of the papers are bent, and the papers are scorched, and burned by the heat of the tears, it is necessary for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it an "injured cure", and it is that you make a scratch on the patient who has this disease the hairs so they have at the front, then make three incisions or at the front equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as if two eyes are entirely in the forehead below, descending to the nose, and the others two on the sides above the papers, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are two on the sides above the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound have a quantity of three fingers at the joints; and apply a piece of sponge and much drapery to suck out the blood, then put the spatula bent at two parts where it is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	Of the incision that is to be made at the temple just up to the second incision; and scrape off all the crust that is between the two fissures to the entire skin that is on the bone, then make another cut of the middle incision just up to the other second, and then extract this spatula-like thing.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put in the first fissure the instrument that is called "scalpel", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the scalpel cutting towards the airy flesh at the heart, and the soft part towards the bone, and the end as far as it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut to the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as far as the incision is continuous up to what opens at the heart, and then make another cut in the middle incision up to the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, and press the flesh for the blood taken; then put in each incision a tent of old cotton, and put on soft drapery soaked in wine and oil and vinegar, and beware that abscesses do not form; and on the third day, loosen the lien, and apply great plantain water, then cure with ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healthy.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes' humour
