Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, take a candle flame, because it is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting on one part, and name on the other part; and when you have cauterized one of the armholes, cauterize the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and hot and easy, and if there is an evacuation of blood, gargle the patient with hot water, or scorchings of green pommes so they are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound is stanched; then cure until it be healthy; and no other time grow in the throat other abscesses than the two armholes, if you cauterize them thus like the two armholes immediately.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, it is to know the small sense of the abscess; and had almost completely closed off the whole throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so large that it had already sent two threads through the two openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then, and thrust in one of the openings, then the thread went further, and drew out a large portion of pus; then I made another attempt through the other opening of the nose, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I thrust the thread into those abscesses, and cut away a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and wine, and did not cease from cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess decreased again, and filled up the space that I had emptied, so much that it became very large; then I deceived her and cauterized within the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I departed from those regions, and knew not what God would do with her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the vein descends into the tube, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round, it is called "tube".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is purified as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit at all, and you see that the painful abscess is appeased, and it is subtle; then it is necessary to cut into it; and the one that is round, assembled, and not long; and it is sanguine or of dark color or black, then it is necessary to avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned before; then put the hook in the tube, and draw it back, and cut around one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two handles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluous flesh which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut too much, it grieves the voice and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the II amandres, and cure until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of cutting, it is necessary that you use gentleness at the cautery of the senses fearing pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of burning with the cautery is sharp and pointed.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient places his head in your healthy hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confides with sharp vivid heat, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the management of this instrument, whose form is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	Here is the translation:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it is with silver or tin, and one of the heads is thrust into the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the vein, so that the eye is mortified; afterwards, you recommence often, until the eye dries out, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of hot abscesses, for many things occur; and do not do it more frequently than at the decline of hot abscesses.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put a piece of egg white in the chief's mouth, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the egg white does not let the vapor pass into the mouth, and it is a good cure, ensuring complete health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens that the gullet or spine of a fish, or something else; thus you should treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun in every instrument, so that you can see the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the gullet, you should make the patient vomit thus so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if it casts out the thing through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of turnip, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and there is the sponge with its filament, and then it transpires; and when it comes to the place, thus it will be; and then you will treat further; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take the instrument of ponching in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they can enter more lightly into the gullet, and hold the head high lifted; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest it does not come to life, nor does it push the bone within; and it is of value that the patient pushes the instrument, because it is seen or the thing is cast out; if it casts out below, or it treats further throughout all the instruments equally, until it is cast out.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the sound of the gullet
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No medicine is suitable for the patient, as I have said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when this does not benefit, then gaze into the patient's throat in the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, if it draws to a small vein, or subtle tendons that hold fast to it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not hold, take a curly-haired cane, and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert or remove the curl of the cane with hot iron, and make it so often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you tighten the patient's water throughout the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full sight of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in as if swallowing, and move it with their hand often; and if soon the wound feels the water, it scabs.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not scab as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with assafoetida, at the instrument that I said in the fumigation of the urine; do this many times, for it will heal without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are visible charcoal, and it is covered with a pierced covering in the middle, and in this perforation is the head of the instrument; then you throw the fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane into his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not exit, but goes up to the sanies; and the sanies will fall now, and if they do not fall, then recommence the fumigation many times; and the patient suffers thirst, and eats salty and bitter things, and drinks no water; and then it is necessary that it be done by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it is, when one can see it, resembles a curved tenaille for entering the throat; and it has the appearance of a beak of a sign, and it has the roughness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the lancets for abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many abscesses are similar, according to what the remembrance comes here after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its own semblance, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is by the eyes where they are at the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce, as long as the bowel is tender according to its accomplishment; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their accomplishment, like abscesses that are near the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and one leaves them until they are ripe inside, perhaps because the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will hurt the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, you should pierce it when it is ripe; and it is not necessary to pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for one that is near the foundation, which does not ripen inward, and becomes fistulous, and cannot be healed in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hole of the perforation of the abscess which is according to its completion, and it is when the pain is appeased, and the departure from fever, and the diminution of the pain and of the redness, and the debate and the settlement of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make sit the perforation or more depending on the abscess, and where it opens mucus; and so the perforation of the long body, and if the abscesses are in hands or feet, or in joints and in veins, and in all equal places where there is no putridity.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that swell, according to the affected limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the raw flesh, if it is necessary that you allow the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce before that, the body will be full of much filth; and by chance they harden the lips and the depths of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limbs have need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many fissures according to the appearance of the greatness of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the skin, and cut; when it has become thus as I describe, and is amortized, it is necessary to do thus as one does for blisters: and if there are those that are cut into three angles, and if there are those that are cut as the foil of myrtle, as abscesses of the entrails; and if there are those where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuttings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Here is the translation:
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expert often kills the patient with the issue of the bowel, which by chance would kill the patient, and you do not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Abandon therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if you evacuate the wound, and examine whether the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain incision, if you apply tents of linen or cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put a tent in each one so they come together; and if you have cut into a part of the skin, and you have shaved around, then it is necessary that you fill with much soft cotton or dressing of linen thread moistened, and leave it just at the third day; then apply ointment, and treat with unction until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you remove blood that has come to the surface, apply cold and still water, and wipe with a cloth, and place it on the limb, washing it many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood removal persists, apply governing treatment and cure, and the powders I mentioned in my book, and if it is winter, and the limbs or abscesses are very nervous, then you must put on warm and oily tents and cloths; and if it is summer, and the limbs are weak, then you must put on cool and oily cloths, or warm and oily wine, until the third day, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and the discharge and the treatment, as it is necessary, until they are healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to cauterize completely in the treatment of abscesses: for you have said how one should proceed beforehand in the treatment of abscesses, and see here this chapter.
des soros	of wounds
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the crust of the wound comes off small abscesses, and there are ways for us that are in bandages, just like the joining of a cut, and many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some fatty ones and such ones where there is moisture also as in the case of pores; and if there are hard and stubborn ones on the incision site, and there is no doubt that the arteries do not act against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the incision site are such that you experience with every instrument called "incisor", from which the shape comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they make it dry by applying pressure from above and along the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, they scrape off everything leaving no skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately if one leaves nothing; then they insert cotton in an Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and in wine, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and they cure what has been delayed from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then recauterize the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain any longer do no harm; then treat the wound of piercing conveniently, so that it be healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses hold in a thick nut, then cut according to this form, from afar; and you scrape your nails, and clear everything around, and put all your treatment of drawing for the cotte where it lies; and if the artery makes you oppose, then do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus do with the abscess if it is pierced, and prune and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the pierced abscess and the moist, if it is less severe, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are some of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and among these were the abscesses that I cut into, or the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a sour, bitter, and white stone, and could not break it; and if one had touched any, one would have done as much harm as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	Here is the translation:
des scrophules	of the tumors
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often it happens that an abscess forms on the neck, and beneath the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come to another part of the body or limb, and are numerous, and are intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly located on its side, like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are those that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	when you see that they are of good disposition on the touchier, and resemble the color of the body, and move from each part and do not stray from the nerve of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and are not too deep; then it is necessary that you cut into them from above, and scrape off each part, and stretch out the two lips of the heart as oncines, if you have mastery, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and pull gently and gently, and be sure that you do not cut into the nerve nor the vein, and are not too shallow, lest you cut into what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut into the vein or artery, and this does not allow you to operate, then put on the wound vitriol ointment, or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound; and let it be until the abscess is calmed, and the wound becomes soft, and begins to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your work, until you complete it; then search with your finger to see if there remain small scrophulae, if you cut and mend them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrophula, it does not behoove you to cut that scrophula at its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself without harm; then fill the wound with much cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire tumor, it is necessary that you reassemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then there will be no more excess flesh due to the greatness of the tumor.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand how to cut at the root of it, and draw out strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those tumors that have excess flesh, pierce where it appears to die; and pierce thus as we said before, depending on the circumstances, then you will mix with ointment and similar things, so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, if the treatment with ointment cures immediately, so that it be healthy.
de squinance	of scalping
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old people said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and it is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have scalping, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cleansed; and one must not do it by aid of this, because all the veins and the pormon of the patient are at risk of having an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the mandrels.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the gullet, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss which comes from the strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it beneath three circles or four with a small cut across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the cut through the syphac, not in the cartilage; and thus it is convenient at the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough to be free.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then cuts the heart as far as it comes to the tonsils; and clears the veins of blood, if you see nothing, and then touches the syphac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the flow of the tonsils which jumps forth from the broken place, and from the lack of voice; and leaves the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound with good care, and sew it whole without sensing the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, so that it be healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	One must not do this just so long as the throat is completely stuffed, and the patient is judged to be mortal, and the defect lacks wings.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then touches the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and for this reason the ancient one commands to leave the wound open as long as the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then they command to sew the wound and cure, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took the cautery, and inserted it in her throat, and touched part of the sinews of her arm; and I was called upon to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discover the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and I saw well that it had not been covered with a bandage nor conducted further than the throat, and the veins were issuing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and cured her until she was healthy; and I didn't find in the maiden any fever except that she was hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition; because it is said that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large gullet
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "throat hernia", and it is a great abscess in the color of a jaundice, and it is very common in women; and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or naturally it has no pain.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two manners, one of which seems like a fat swelling, and the other manner seems like an abscess that comes from the artery; and there is fear, and it does not seem possible to operate on those who are small, and prove and search everywhere: if you find it thus as I said gras, and it does not go into any vein, if you cut, if you cut them as one cuts the veins, and draw it out of its entirety, if there is no point; and search well everywhere, and cure it as it seems, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of the nose
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways for us to heal, of which I will describe all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I explain the entire difference between them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the illness is heat and fever, as long as the inflammation has passed, and it completes the purification; then restore the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the patient having no heat nor fever nor pain, and containing yellow bile, which is their own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins thus like a jaundice, and becomes thick; and are according to these similarities, whether grave, or moist, and much of the color is as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the wound, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to what its shape will come or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into the abscesses of the wounds is that you take or make the moist place where you find it in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instruments have perceived the core, then according to the greatness of the abscess; then extract the suppurating matter, and take care not to force too much.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	Here is the translation:
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it stays nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it stays a little, and the wound does not grieve you, if you apply some corrosive powders to the wound, and hold the wound steady, and put soothing things on the hot abscess, and treat other wounds until it is healthy; and if the wound is great, so sew up the lips of the wound, and treat what bothers you.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is beating strongly against your hand or another, and you hasten to employ the virtue of broken vitriol, and let it stay two or three days, until the wound suppurates, and then restore the ebullition of blood; then return to cauterize what has been left behind.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of inserted instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quadrants which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula; and they are also like the needles with which one sews up the sores, and are made of citrin, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more experienced for sewing up black pustules; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the largeness of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of onions are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are onions that have two curvatures in three ways also; and if there are onions that have three curvatures, and are also of three ways; and if there are onions that have two curvatures, and onions with a single curvature only, and are of three ways; and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these instruments is sharp, and there are those that do not cut more than one part, from which the nails are scraped, because one does not cut into the vein or nerve; and these introductors are the lancets placed in the hands, so that the patient does not feel it at the opening of the abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them no more than in the charnut, such as legs, arms, and limbs, and similar places; and never do they make another small instrument, resembling scrapers of fistulae, according to this form, at which blood is staunched.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and he puts it back into its place that joins the veins, and the arteries, and it does not return according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Here is the translation:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Here is the translation:
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses of the sitting bones
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from beneath the sitting bones are kinds of hard scrofulous tumors or they have ribs, and if there is only moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be treated according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire abscess is emptied, fill the wound with much cotton, and let it be until another day, then remove all the cotton, and heal by applying ointment so that it becomes healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, do so as we have said in cases of scrofula, and if the wound becomes hollow, apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is injured, and the skin is swollen which is above, then often come abscesses, and it also happens to the inflamed vein with an abscess; and if you recognize thus that it is because of the artery, then the abscesses are long in depth; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel the strangeness; and when it is because of the vein, then there are obvious signs appearing; and it is foolish to try to remove this abscess, and also when it is under the muscles and near the bones and in the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it is necessary to abandon the treatment with iron, and the one who is at the head must also abandon it, and in the one who is inflamed by an artery make a incision above the skin of the affected limb; then open the incision as wide as possible, and carefully separate the artery from the surrounding tissue, until it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath, and make it pierce to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then touch the place which is between the two ligatures of an intromission, so that the blood flows out, and the abscess is freed; then apply the treatment that induces a crisis, until the ligature is cut; then treat what is coming from the incision, until it is healthy; and if the abscess is due to the vein, you must hold with your hand what you can of the abscess under the entire skin, then insert the needle underneath the place you are holding, and make it pierce, and use a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have told you, or the ligature of one of the two parts of the artery; and if you doubt that the thread is not firm, you reinsert another needle through all the threads underneath the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in three places; then touch the abscess until the superfluity flows out, then touch the superfluous part of the artery and leave what is tied; then put on a soft cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply treatments with tents and ointments until it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the kidneys
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Here is the translation:
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And it happens more often to the joints and the two and in all the joints where they have joints, and it's the grief of apostemes, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many dispositions without pain; and when one strains it forcefully, the patient feels pain, and it's not at all in the depth of the body, but beneath the skin; and it moves well from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor beneath nor above, and he who is in joints does not want to be treated with iron: by chance it would cause contraction; and he who is at the head or forehead, makes the skin spasm.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the apostemes are small, hold them with tongs, and cut at their root; and if they are large, suspend them from the ankle, and scrape, then oste and assemble the wound to the suture, and cure until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	of large bulging swellings
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Here is the translation:
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weigh them and found in one 18 ounces heavy, and in the other 6 ounces, and the work in the incision is that you examine if the patient's moistures are wet, and the color of the joint is pale and moist and of subtle root; if you apply the spatula large, and be in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Because the blood-letter comes too frequently with great evacuations of blood, and if you do not have the skill, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient fearing and anxious about the incision of the iron, take a well-made thread, and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease from restraining the thread until it reaches the joint, and thus works without trouble; and if the roots are large, fear not to cauterize in the middle of the belly, but you can well cauterize most of it, then cauterize so it does not return; then cure the wound, and beware that you do not cauterize the thin skin which is of false color and of poor sense and of little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of encrusted sores later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling is full
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the abscess comes from fire cautery or breaking of the skin, and it is on the belly and in some of the skin folds, as if it had been caused by other injuries, or blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or windiness; and if it is due to the breaking of the skin and issuing of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens with diverse discharge.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses with their fingers if it swells up, and then returns, and sometimes it is narrow, and increases much at the entry of the bath and through strong effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press on it with your hand, it does not constrict at all; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the operations are that you examine whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It seems necessary to let the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in this chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, then it is necessary to instruct the patient to hold their belly, and be straightened out entirely, then sign across the navel; then instruct them to sit between your hands, then go across the place you have signed all around the spatium; then bind it with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and hold the limb steady; then uncover half of the abscess extended over the limb, and touch your index finger, and feel the intestine; if you find it taken by the limb, then release it, and put the intestine back in its place; and if you find the bowel, take it to the navel, and cope with the superfluity; and if the artery or the vein does something against you, go gently across, then return to your work and take two needles, and thread them with a strong cord, and thread the two needles in what you have done in a cross that you have made pierce; then stretch the abscess across four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and let the belly heal as much as it can, and expel the dead flesh by itself; or cope with it when it is subtle and porous, then cure what is necessary, and dress the abscess as we have said; and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the belly of what is necessary, and repair the belly.
dou chancre	two ulcers
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken in the division of similar ulcers, and how one should operate with medicines, and how one should avoid the cure with iron; and we say that an ulcer is in the marrow, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when an ulcer is in the limb or where it can be reached if it is like an ulcer which is in the muscles, and in the skin, and in similar places, and one should remove everything when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it does not matter that you approach it, for I cannot heal any of them; nor did anyone ever heal them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in the limb or where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile several times; then make them healthier if they show manifest repletion, then make the patient healthy before doing the operation; then cut off your ulcers or cancers, and shave all parts, and scrape all parts without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and carefully feel the limb with your hand or with something else, and see that the remaining blood does not contradict the incision of the artery or vein, so cauterize until the blood is stanched; then cure with another cure until it is healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Here is the translation:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cutting of two parts.

des pustules de la verge	the pimples on the rod

de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Here is the translation:

dou retenement de l’urine	due to retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.
