de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stones, and their extraction with medicines; and I have told the difference between stones in the kidneys as they fall, and all the signs, and in which stone one must operate with a cut; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the bladder often falls in children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder with subtle signs; and it appears suddenly, and greatly troubles the patient's penis, and they urinate frequently, and then become constipated; and most of these symptoms are the foundations; and it's easy to cure children until they are three years old, and it's very difficult in old people, and it's as if it's a middle age, for those who are between youth and old age; and it's easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to clean the patient through evacuation, in order to expel all the bad humors that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders the recovery of the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift them up and move them downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and often falls down from the high place; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downward; then touch and feel inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall to the toucher from everything, if you move your right index finger of the left hand, if the patient is old, or your left middle finger, if the patient is young and accomplished; and feel its foundation, and touch the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and feel at the limit where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch out his right hand above the loins, and with his left hand to clear the skin which is under the loins in the area where one makes the incision; then he puts on the spatula-like instrument, so that it is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between this which is between the hip and the fundament, not in the middle but at the side of the left thigh; and be straight on the stone, and both feet are thus or foundation, and be the girth of the traversing so it is large by default, and within is narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too great; perhaps the press if both feet which is or foundation, that it feels beneath the labor; and knows that there is a part of the stone where it has angles, and margins: if it is heavy to extract; and if there is a part which is underneath, similar to a ball, and rounded, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If the stone has angles and margins, make the girth larger; and if it does not come out, then you must extract it with pincers that are like a lime at the head, for extracting the stone so it doesn't escape; or you put beneath it an instrument subtly curved at the head; and if you cannot engineer it thus, then enlarge the little passage, and if the blood does not flow, then extract with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, then remove first the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cope with, then pull strongly, and the small ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it needs to be treated with care, and to make a bigger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Because these things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes back through the wound that the abscess cannot suppurate; but in any case you make an effort to treat it, or to break up the tendons, so that you treat it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, if you apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it steady, and put on top a dressing of soft oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the hot abscess; then reposition the patient on his back, and do not undo the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, rub in very well the oil and water, then apply the ointment of galenon and ointment of basilicon, until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses come in the wound and corrode, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by this means that the urine is known to exit in such a way without a sound with the urine: then put your finger in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and putrefy; then lift the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and aid him in all ways that you know, so that he may be healthy; and it is necessary that all the holes that you cure, you tie the two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the spot.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is conducted by the rod, and fixed in, and the urine cannot flow out; if you cure this as I say thus, that you repeatedly cut many times, it is excused from cutting through this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a forest of iron according to this form and be at two angled points fixed in the thigh:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and wind it around the rod beneath the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then insert the thread into the rod gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the thread with your hand in the stone little by little, until you can feel the stone from another part; if the urine comes soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is within the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this because of something that deflects it, then place the thread beneath the stone and another above, then make the rod straight over the stone between the two threads, then extract it, and undo the thread, and cleanses the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure until it is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Because the stone is often found in women, and if it happens at any time, then the treatment is grievous, and is defended by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows herself well, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third method is that sometimes one cannot find a woman who knows well this art of hands; and the fourth method is that the stones of the woman are more profound than those of the man, because it needs to make deeper cuts, and great fear is there. And if you need to ascend to this, then you must take a wise midwife, and grasp the true vein on, and if you do not find one, then ask for a subtle test; and present a wise old woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and instruct her to do what you command from the inquiry into the stones; and observe very well if the woman is a virgin: then she must thrust her finger or foundation and search for the stones; and if she finds them, then constrict beneath her finger, and recommend that she thrusts her finger or with the malady, and squeezes and presses her left hand on the bladder strongly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it is necessary to move the skin from the entrance of the bladder up to the root of the thigh, so that it reaches the base of the thigh; then press on the stone in the root of the thigh against the soft confluence, where it appears misplaced, and feels the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above the stone or below, and let the wound be at first small; then put the ointment on the wound, if you feel the stone if it increases the pain so much that the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: it is to know, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you recognize the symptoms in order to know the disease.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the wound does not heal, set on it a vitriol ointment, and hold it for an hour so that the wound is stained; then return to your work, until the stone comes out, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the stone as remedies to aid you in your operation; and if the wound does not heal, and it is from the artery that was cut, set powder on the wound and bind with bandages and compresses, and do not start again, and leave the stone alone, lest by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the veins are purified, so return to your work, until the stone is loosened.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The watery humor is nothing other than a mixture of moisture or white syrup, which is beneath the skin of the hips, containing the egg-white; and it is called "syrup", and sometimes it is properly in the web of the egg-white, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the hip between the white syrup that we have said; and this does not happen rarely.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this remedy is from weakness that comes to the joints, and it spreads out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: whether it's declining yellow to jaundice, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and that happens more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is or becomes white as we have said, the abscesses are ripe, I don't think it takes long like the figure of an egg, and doesn't open the joints, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own membrane, the abscesses are ripe with part of the egg, and therefore one thinks that it's another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white surface, then it feels very well; thus when you want to know the color of the moisture, you should try all the inner quarters, from which the form is presented before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the internal parts, judge from what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the fullness of his body; then he should sit on his back, on something slightly elevated, and much drapery is placed under him; then he sits on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on his right, and extends the rod to one of the two ribs of the heart; then take the spatula in hand, and cut the skin of the ribs through the length of the loin up to the point where it touches, and make a straight incision in cutting the skin of the ribs just to the white skin, and carefully remove the skin according to his power; then pierce the white skin plain with water, and extract all the water, and then put on ointments, and apply the white skin above; and do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only the white skin; cut out all or in pieces, if you do not cut it well subtly, the white skin will return; and if the ulcer becomes inflamed because of your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the white skin; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the ribs to one bandage, then treat it like the other wounds, until it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the vein corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to ligate the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then cut the joint at all the suspensions, and extract the vein, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; if you cut the other part as you did the first equalization, then let out the blood, and put on the painful wound a gentle ointment made with rose oil; and put on another gentle ointment made with wine and oil, and put on the two gauzes, and put double drapes over it, and bind everything together according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two gauzes and fill them with lint in this way, and assemble them by stitching at the throat of the arm, and one of the heads takes hold at the base just to the back, and another at the part of the finger; and another head on the two angles, and so everything is assembled in the loop of the arm; and no medicine is made with this cautery iron rod, and it is that you take a subtle cautery scalpel, and cut the skin of the gauzes, and be careful as we have said, so that the white syrup that contains the wound is uncovered; if you take the cautery in this way, and pierce that white syrup as with onyx, and scrape it with this subtle hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And you should burn in all the ways that you can, as much as you stretch everything; and beware that the fires do not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salutary; and beware of the deterioration of blood, and dread the operations of cutting; and if nothing makes you counter, or abscess bursts or deteriorations of blood or another thing, cure what makes you counter, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to attend to this operation due to its horribleness, so perform perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that the watery fluid is there, so make the patient sit on a high seat; then pierce the abscess in the thick part of the whole spatula large, and put the perforation from a long cord; and let the openings be wide, so that all the watery fluid flows out; then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and leave to flow the remainder of the watery fluid, then cure until the wound is healthy; and if the white fabric does not let the watery fluid issue from the mouth of the wound, it is necessary that you use a pipe or instrument with which one draws the watery fluid from the hydropics, so that its form is thus before; and enlarge the wound, and know that the watery fluid returns, and is assembled after six months or within a year, and when it is assembled as before, then the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the loins
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Here is the translation:
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come from corruption, and similarly from wounds; and it is in most cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by excessive and bitter sharpness, which spreads to the joints, or from percussion; and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no finding of pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and by chance some abscesses are greenish and pungent, and of bad color, and sometimes they come from a narrowing of the artery, or from an inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to a narrowing of the artery, it is recognized by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press on it with your fingers; and it does not seem that you should touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those that are made from an inflammation of the vein are recognized by their disposition to the expression of finger touch, and one can well take the measure on this similarity, and on the other parts; and it is that you cut out the kernel of the joints, then the egg-white rises high, and the traitor flees from the white skin, and delivers the suspension from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is suddenly swollen with these new wounds, then it is necessary that you treat the vein, and the wound; and if it is higher up at the ankle, or in those which are beneath the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all this tension, and the wound rounds again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is where the skin is at the back, then it is necessary that you cut all of it, and extract the humor, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the operations are accomplished, then apply the plaster of lime and rose oil and wine, then treat with other treatments until he is healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the loins
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	These are enveloped abscesses with an envelopment similar to a scorpion's tail, with the softening of the surrounding areas, and the patient suffers greatly when they walk; and the treatment of this disease is very close to being fearful as it was before, and we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you seat the patient on a high chair, then bind them with suspensories of linen threads below their two arms, to all the vessels which are near the edge, and tie the master veins, and extend them forcibly; then cut into the spatula trenchantly and widely through the area where the vessels are discovered, and then strip away from each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then fix a needle or thread with double twist, and bind it to the first joint or where the veins come together, and bind it again at the other end; then bind them in the middle directly, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moistures; then treat the wound as the others do, so that no vessel shrinks away from nourishing one of the vessels; for by this means no harm comes, and if all the vessels come together, it is necessary to treat the vessels at every point; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the treatment of this face
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	Here is the translation:
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a section of pus, which brings about sudden severe pain at its onset, and it is the diverse appearances of abscesses beneath the skin, close by, and it is due to the issue of the intestine and the body being worn out by the pus.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it settles beneath the ribs with the intestine, and is retained there, and causes great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with iron to fear, because they think it will scare them away.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Here is the translation:
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is the cautery of the swelling veins, as we have said, after the incision, due to doubt about the removal of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the abscess form until it bursts of its own accord; and if it delays in ripening, then apply warm water, and put on what we have said, until it bursts; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healthy.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case I never saw anyone who could make the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the old ones said that it is done like the scythe that is assembled near the vein, in such a way that you tie the veins, after cutting lightly underneath; then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess with what opens, until the veins heal; and treat as we have said, until it is perfectly healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and opens the veins; and do not descend into the intestines with any coils, and if you do, it is little, and repair all hours; and always if it stays too long at this point, the wound or siphac will swell, until the intestine descends; and this happens by extending the siphac that is in the groin, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and enlarged the veins and opened; and the treatment is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way: and it is that the patient lies supine on their back between your hands, then cut the vein of the rupture swollen from the large according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the siphac that is beneath the skin which is inflamed, then take the rait and put it on the apparent vein of the siphac; and press at the bottom of the belly, then cut the two apparent veins of the siphac on the head of the rait, and cut one and the other; then extract the head of the rait, and do not touch any point of the siphac that does not extend to another thing, as I have made you know in the treatment of the rupture of the intestines; then treat with the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the veins, if it is wounded and cures the wound, so that it may be healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The abscess is constricted, and has no appearance in the wound, and the cauterizations are moved in this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the groin
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the groin is softened in some men, because the flesh that is within is mollified, and it is a pleasure to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure, to make the patient sit on his back, and cover the softened skin with natural skin; then assemble the .ij. lips to a suture, and if you see, cut first the superfluous soft skin at .iij. sutures or .iiij. firmly; then cover between the sutures, and cure it like other wounds, until it is healthy, and sews the thread.
dou chastrement	of punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	It is known that cauteries are mentioned in our law, and for this reason I prefer not to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to force them except by two means: one is that the masters respond in writing when asked about the cure; and the other, because we often have need of cauterizing certain beasts to aid us, such as goats and sheep and cattle and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cauteries are made according to two methods: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we make by attraction, we seat the beast in warm water, until the skin is softened and pendulous; then take them with your hand, until they are reset and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Here is the translation:
des hermofrodites	and the hemorrhoids
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Here is the translation:
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another way is with women, and it is on the little finger as if a rod and they bind.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of a man and a woman is that you dress the wounded parts all together, and the treatment is like other wounds; in the second way, for men whose urine jumps through the skin of the loins, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tents of the genitals
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tentigen is a wounded part on the natural area, as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the tentigen to your hand or to the onions, and dress lightly; and do not go too deeply in fear of causing a flow of blood, then the treatment of another wound until it is healthy; and there is another wound that grows at the mouth of the marsh, and the example, and by chance it jumps forth, and it is similar to the appearance of a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to operate, as we have said concerning the inflammation, and the treatment so that it may be healthy.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is an error if the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the pertus is small; and it is natural from birth, or accidental due to illness that has come; or it is by chance ajostee, or subtle dou syfac, and it is made deep in the marrow, or in the sides, or below, or whatever; and it prevents conception, and infant development, and by adventure the flowers have; and the knowledge of this is by the examination of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the symptoms are approaching quickly, then look at your fingers or in the vein.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is subtle dou syfac, and it is approaching as the liver, then hurry, and arrange thus: put your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs; then stretch out the two livers formally, so that the subtle dou syfac may be rounded, and overcome the symptoms; then take a thread, and wind it in oil, and put it on the spot, and guide the woman to each house every day, so that she cannot conceive.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the skin is hard and thick, it is necessary to apply cupping glasses similar to a foil of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscesses are of new flesh, then suspend an onion and a cup; and among the medicines that staunch blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and ensemble abundant water; then apply a large poultice of soft cloth, so that the wound cannot suppurate; and thus it will be lengthy, and apply a tent of dry linen; then be cured by other cures until it is healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when new flesh appears in the wound, then it is necessary to cover according to this method, if there are no abscesses that become inflamed.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that becomes inflamed in the wound should not be touched with iron.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are overgrowths of veins that without sharp custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thellu; and we have already said in the division the similarities to those, and the signs, and I will tell you here those that receive curation.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the thigh, when they are deeply rooted in the marrow, and do not appear to the sense, if it is not the cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the marrow, which one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then stretch out the thigh as tendons, and cut into its roots, then powder on medicines that stop blood flow, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bathe her feet in a cold bath for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if the blood comes out, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and of galls and similar things, and then take oat flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and apply it as a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he is steady, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him straighten his back and arms without striking; then take a lancet, and apply the juice of plantain or of angelica with old wine, and make him straight.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess breaks, heal the wounded place so it is healthy; and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough-headed chief, so you must cover it as I have said before; and then heal until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come to the marrow, such as cancer and piercing abscesses and herpes and stitches and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary therefore that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess which comes to the marrow, which is not like the abscesses that collect pus; and if you want to know the work of iron, look if the abscess is agitated at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make the patient wait until the pain is alleviated; and then have the patient sit on a chair, and let him lean against his back and assemble his feet as parts of a broken limb; and let his thighs be spread out, and put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a linen bandage; then suck out the swelling from the right side, and prepare the instrument by which one opens the mouth of the marrow, so that afterwards the form appears; and it is necessary that when you have prepared this instrument, you make a first trial to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters from the instrument does not come more than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instruments are larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with drapes, so that the instruments do not harm; and it is necessary that he puts the cornet of the instrument on top, and holds the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one makes a poultice with the softest part of the hand, if it is necessary to cover the head, at the gentle touch; and when the wound is empty, if it is necessary to put ten moist applications in rose oil or green oil; and put the application firmly on the wound at the edge of the marrow, and put it under the marrow and on the clean skin, netting with a subtle or mediocre skill so they may be treated; then heal afterwards, within two days of applying, as long as it is healthy; and never lift the marrow and the wound by cleansing with water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and aristological treatment so they may be treated; then return to the application.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed in the marrow, it is necessary to guard against cauterizing with iron, but rather treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of the birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Here is the translation:
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it happens sometimes upon his feet, and comes to the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes to his belly, or swelling, and is turned by bad luck around his neck, and by other evil figures; if it is necessary for the patient to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes onto its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the virtues of it are weak, then make her sit on a chair, or where the women hold her; and let her nature be of oil or fenugreek which is cooked, and then put the baby between her two little spatulas, which is its form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and feel the second one, and touch his finger as much as the moisture that is in the running flux; and take hold of the belly of the woman as much as the children are descending, and if they do not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman of muscillaige of fenugrec with oil of sisament; then make her take a purging draught and be confined for a condition, and keep her mouth and nose an hour: if now the children come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands are swollen, it is necessary that you reset them gently little by little; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet high up; then remove the chair from the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when getting up; and if the hands cannot enter, and the infant dies, cut the hands at the cutting board that is placed before you, and extract the child, and reset evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, it is necessary to lift them up high; and then turn them little by little, until they are even; then take one of the feet and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps just to the hips, instruct to take hold, and make them straighten with good sense; if it is swollen, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump far as we have said, then turn it a little and a little, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, take a poultice of heated wine, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and pound everything in the mortar; and place it on the woman's nature within and remove this ointment, then make her sit in hot water until beneath the ribs; and when she is softened beneath, make her wear a belt of myrrh, and put it beneath, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the chair, then make her sneeze and hold her nose and mouth, and take her belly lightly, for now the infant will come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the escape of the child onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse. de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the issue of the child on its neck, and it has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back

de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Here is the translation:

de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is necessary that the balm knows all this, for it happens that similar things have occurred; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; and the minister should anoint her hands with oil made from athelia and fenugrec and flaxseed, then apply the bandage to her arms with these oils and muscillaiges; then put them lightly in the marrow, then take the child out of there, or she takes out what is conceived there, and appears to be born on her chief; if you fix the nails in her eyes or in her neck or in her mouth or in her palace or under her beard or in her strength or near her ribs, and it is born on her feet, then fix or prick them and cut through her sides; and it is necessary that she holds the nail with her right hand, and puts the curve between the fingers of her left hand, and applies it lightly to her whole hand, and fixes the nail in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then you find another bone, where the third is in a similar position, so that the extractions are even; and then they are evenly set in motion from one part to another, to issue forth, and the bones are held firmly, so it's like this is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if it remains in one part, then anoint the boil with some of its oily drops, and apply them to that part, and treat the other part; and if it does not remain at all, then put this bone or higher up, and do thus until it issues forth completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be reduced by stretching, then you must wrap around the drapil, until it issues forth completely; then put a bandage on the joint of the foot or at the heel, and thus you must do with the other hand, and so for the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is twisted in the exit, or if it has an assembled sharp chief, it is necessary that you insert the spinal spatula between your two, and make the chief and extract the sharpness; or you rotate it to the instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with the instruments or chapter which follows this one; and thus the same makes the children have a large natural chief; and then treat the bones as tenailles, and if the head breaks out and it holds to the forceps, so be careful that the moisture which is in the worst exit; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces at the joint where you can; and if it is stuck in the belly or below the ribs, it is necessary that you pull as far as the moisture corrodes.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the infant is on its feet, it is light attraction, and the adjustments at the mouth of the marrow are lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is twisted in the belly or at the breast, it is necessary that you extract it with the drapil enveloped on the hand; and make the belly or breast, as far as the moisture which corrodes there; and if the other limbs are oiled, and the head remains, put the bail in your hand in front of the marrow, and treat just up to the mouth of the marrow; then you put I or II, and treat again; and if the mouth of the marrow is constricted by a hot abscess which has come, do not bother to work, but rather prepare moist and greasy things; and the administrator places enemas, and thus in soft mollifying and moisturizing.

And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, so amend what we have said about the living infant; and if one cannot do it, so let it be treated in parts, and leave nothing of the secondary.

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly an infant had been dead, then she conceived another on top of that, and rejected the other dead one.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, a swelling came to his abdomen, and it inflamed so much that it opened, and began to discharge greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the case, and I thought for a long time, and could not soothe the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong plaster, and it drew out a bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled greatly, because this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I touched the wound, and I inserted my hands so far that the woman was in a better state; and I examined the woman at length thus, and I sucked out a little of the bad humor from the wound; and I did not recall this chapter further except for what, when the masters find an extraordinary thing, they know how to put it to use.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the hammer back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the pressor, where one weighs the books; and at 10 turns as 10 heads of the ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes. Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Here is the translation:
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all elevated above, and are multiplied in their similarities; and when the mirrors have them aligned, so much the more hasty is the work, and higher are the homes according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not aligned, for its necessities are not excusable.

When the secondine is retained in infancy, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold their wing, and then make them steady with condition, and hold their hands at the mouth and nose; and if they cough through this, it is good.

If not, take the pot, and make a pertus or covercle, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marris, such as calmant, rue, anise, camomile, cassialigne, and centoire; all these herbs, or some of them, being cooked or poached in water over the fire; then put a cane or pertus in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marris, and hold it as long as the vapors come out of the marris; then make them steady, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second inflammation hurries.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and is not yet feverish, instruct the patient to anoint their left hand with oil of sesament or muscillaige of altee, and then put it in the nature, and seek the secondine; and when they have found it, take it and stretch it little by little straightly, so that the marris does not slip at the extraction; but it is necessary to move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then draw; if it comes and disentangles.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is constricted, we have said that the treatment involves cleansing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not respond to everything we have said, beware that you do not cause harm in the treatment; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the womb, you apply it to the cervix of the woman, then cliterize with four-drug ointment; if she takes it and recovers, and becomes fertile again; however, when she conceives, a bad smell comes from the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Here is the translation:
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument is thus, where one fumes the woman at the retention of the flowers and of the second one, this is it.
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like seeing a dog, and placing the subtle head in its natural state, and widening the jaws over the fire; and let there be fumigation on the coals, and the tincture until it is exhausted, and recommencing another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not received the foundation perceived, thus it is obstructed by subtle suffocation: so it is necessary to apply a poultice that perceives this subtlety with its finger, and does not touch the spatula of ague, and guards the ligament so it does not touch; then place on a warm linen cloth soaked in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until it is healthy.

And if you doubt that it does not stiffen, then put or apply a plaster of lead, and leave it on for many days, and let it be removed when the infants want to go to their chambers.

And sometimes suddenly comes this swelling of wound or abscess; if it is necessary to cut into that sudden thing: if it is cured, as we have said about the treatment of a painful blow.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the bottom
