It is necessary that you cut this joint, so that the toe repaires according to its natural forms; then put between two tender or moistened drapes in rose oil, so they do not stick together; or you put between two pieces of subtle plaster, until the toe is stuck, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	They stick to one of these two with the palm, if you see that sticking, as it is necessary.
des vils	of the hairs
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	They are large, swollen veins full of superfluous melancholic humors that come into many members of the body; and more often they occur in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer sometimes a purging of the colon, and then the juice of the basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is in two manners: one is that they cut, and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The surgical incision is in this manner: first raise the leg to a hot and very strong fire, so that the gross blood is subtitled, then stretch the leg of the patient from above the thigh just to the part below the knee; then cut the vein at one, two, or three places with a large incision, then release and draw out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other, until as much blood has been released as the virtue of the patient can suffer; and then let it be, and command that they abstain from eating black-colored food; and recommence the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and annoy the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and tangled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must bend it straight, but do not cut it; and pull it as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut, so it does not cut the vein; and it is of thick curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but being large as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is engendered in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs nor tree grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this comes from the putrefaction that arises beneath the skin, as it comes from the serpent-like and worm-like courses, engendering between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes into the leg, then it changes the veins, and begins to issue forth like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of wood, two and a half inches long, and the nut, and leave the wood on the leg, and every time it does not reach the depth, if you wrap around the wood, and the nut; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut into its root, until it is all issued; for if you cut into it, it returns to the flesh, and causes an abscess or putridity in the limb, and great illness; because it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains in the course; and it often happens with this vein when it is treated with five palms long, or ten, and a few men came to me who had it issued from ten palms long, and when you cut into it, it bursts forth like a root, and pierces deeply, so that everything issues forth; and let the matter that is inside be emptied, and administer medicines to prevent putridity any day, then cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And many times at this vein of the hand, and likewise when it opens in the joint of the foot, or of the foot itself, and a lot of pus comes out, and from which it springs; cauterize the wound thus as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of wounds that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "ox disease", because it often has ox-like swellings, and it is a small wound that grows between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, ascending and descending, and one feels it well as it spreads from member to member, until it destroys the skin or it breaks out; and it is caused by putridity of certain humors, like worms and serpents and lice and ascariases in the belly; and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it reaches the eye, by chance it returns, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you want to cure and treat, if one cannot force it when it goes: then it is necessary that you bind the limb above and below with a strong lien tightly, then cut into and treat forcefully, and if the verse is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you do not find it, if you cauterize with fire above, until it dies; and the greatest harms it does, if it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, hold it firmly below with a formed brow, then cut into, and treat forcefully; and it is necessary to use the patient's mundification of bodily medicine solutives for the bad humidors porries, and beware of eating rotten food in putridity.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the arm; and I soon saw it swell up like a vein at the shoulder, faster than anything, like living silver when it flows from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then soon spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it turned back into her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed how it moved in this way from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had wanted to know more about how the pain moves from one place to another, but I did not know, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and therefore appeared constrained; and it did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and restored veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you want to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, it should appear as we have said, if the vein above and below is hastily opened, and then cut into it so that the constriction of the vein is relieved; and cauterize the vein; and if you do not see with your eyes, treat what drives out the constrictions, like fetid pills, and serpent pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Here is the translation:
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and notched ones, and soldered ones; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those where there are pieces; and one which falls in no principal member falls according to many ways: whether in a principal member it notches, like the head, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls into no place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about afterwards, appears: if it happens that you extract this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not deeply set, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when the arrowhead is in it and pierces the bone, and then the syncope falls who is above the brain, are stuttering and swooning and turning upside down in eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and perturbation of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it loses the function of the nostrils, or of the ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and then there is a whitish moist wound resembling a pustule, and then it also resembles a bruise of flesh; and if these signs appear, then attend to the cure, and pull out the arrowhead if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seat when it falls on the heart, is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in a hard thing, not soft; and by chance the seat moves as the pulse, and in short black blood, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: be aware then without doubt that death draws near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow wound that never leaves the forearm are that without flatulence, it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and breathes deeply and quiets the frosty air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead sticks in the covering of the piss, it is beneath the small ribs; and casts great anguish and great pain and breathes; and moves all the members of the loins.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if it happens to him that his stomach or stomach hurts, perhaps because of jumping from an injury something undigested in the food.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if it happens to him that his stomach or belly hurts, and there is a blockage in the intestine, if there is no hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the obstruction.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if it happens to him that his bladder hurts, and the urine jumps and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulders and the joints and the spine of the back and the arms and the hips and the legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to several different dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the vein is in a tender nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, thus I will tell you that it happened to me, because you should do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that a vein broke out at the root of the nail: I touched it, and drew it from another part beneath the fat of the ear, and was without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I drew out a vein that broke in the fat of the eye beneath the skin, and the vein was bent back, and could not be touched except at the point towards the hollow, and it was a large vein like a Turkish bow, all the way to the iron leg without ears; the game was successful, and no bad accidents happened to me.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I pulled a shaft from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic shaft to the ears: I seized the bristles, and subtle as I pulled, and the Christian was cured.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled a shaft from the man, which was stuck in his belly, and I thought he would die; and then after thirty days had passed, it did not move from its position; I cut around the shaft, and extracted it, and pulled it out strongly, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if I saw a man with a shaft fallen into his back, and the wound was sewn up over it; and the shaft remained inside him, and did not change its natural disposition, nor did I find harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, who had a shaft fall into his face, and the wound was sewn up; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated a wound on the hand of the prince's king, which was stuck in his nail, and it was slightly declining towards the right side; and the wound was completely healed. I was called to care for him after he had been wounded for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched for it with a subtle touch, and did not feel it; and he felt a sharp pain and ache beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I put on the place a plaster attractive and digestive, because the wounds did not swell; and the appearance of the wound showed itself to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in bed for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead one day within his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put the medicine on the wound with corrosive power for many days, until it was open, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow which had stuck in the flesh; then I applied the opening of the wound with that medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and it traversed well the terminals for three months, and then relaxed if the wound that I had put the tongs, and the flesh on one side and the other, and could not issue; then I did not cease to subtly and ingeniously use devices, until I took it out one day with well-made tongs, according to what its form would come at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the mirror showed that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Here is the translation:
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not enter the limbs where they are fixed unless in two ways: either by the direction of the limb or they enter, or from another part; and the one that enters through the flesh, it is an arrow entering into the muscles, and it does not enter now for the first time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not enter now, let it be until the flesh is purified around, and the issue is alleviated; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot exit, let it be thus for some days, and the swelling decreases each day; and then it enters, and if it does not enter, if you pierce around with a subtle finger, as much as the flesh around is enlarged, and then pull.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes just up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and none of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not pull it out, but let it be until it is even after some days, for if the arrow comes just up to the forehead, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed in the bone under the socket, and does not come just to the surface, and the patient remains several days without bad accident, so the engine of two treatments.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very firmly fixed and cannot come out, administer tareres around it, as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the flesh of the body so that one cannot see it, if it has taken all its tension; and if you feel it, if you draw it out with no suitable instrument; and if you cannot do so due to the narrowness of the wound, and due to the depth of the arrow, and there is neither bone nor nerve, if it seems as though the wound is large; and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears where it holds, if you remove the flesh that is embedded in two parts as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, so that you can extract it; and be careful not to break the arrow, that you may extract it more grievously.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at one time, then leave it until the surrounding tissue is purified, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the blood flow counteracts, so amend what we have said about the cure in this chapter; and beware of the incision into the nerve and vein, and do not trust how you can easily remove the arrow without danger, whether it is sharp or dull, or firm or loose; and place the patient according to the form they were in when the arrow fell on them, for that is the greatest aid, and if you cannot, so arrange according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it appears with nothing of its own, or the skin is swollen in that place if one sees or feels it: cut down then, as much as the tongs can grasp, and then extract it: if it does not come out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly, as much as it enters into the bone, and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the residue of the arrow is there, push it all the way through; and if the residue breaks, and you need to administer a push, if you administer an instrument with a curved end, so that the point of the arrow enters the curve of the instrument; and then push it out, and if the arrow is curved, push the instrument in with its point entering inside, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the veins are, so you can, then heal the wound as it convalesces.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls in the foot or in the belly or in the bladder or in the ribcage, and it is near the surface, and you can cut above it, so you cut; and beware of cutting into a vein and a nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, as is necessary; and heal until it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they are made in many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the instrument for cutting is like the claw of an eagle, to cut at the point of the arrow, as it is the shape.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for cauterizing and for scaling if it is so:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one bleeds, of which there are XVI in the head, to know: two that are behind the ears, called "herbech"; and two arteries that are in the temples apparent; and two veins that are in the eyebrows, called "aspires"; and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the back of the nose; and the two gullies that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly sained in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the chest, and people call it "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side of the chest, and people call it "vein of the belly", and it is near the armpit, and it is the one that is sained, which appears manifestly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the auricular and anular, and has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the curve of the pouch on the left side of the chest, and the second is at the ankle on the right side of the chest; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Here is the translation:

Here is the translation:
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sanity of the vein at the forehead is worth as much as the sanity of the cephalic as ancient maladies of the face, and in migraine, and in redness; and the quality is that the patient strains his neck twisting, so much that the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this shape:

And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see; then release the patient's neck, and hold the vein until it is healthy and never again inflamed from a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Here is the translation:
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The sanity of the two veins that are in the two arms helps with the eyes, and in the tongue, and in redness, and in the corner of the eye, and as maladies of the face; and the quality of their sanity is that the patient strains his neck twisting without any strain, as before; then it heals, and so the sanity of the crossing, a little above the long flame a little large, for there is no point of flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien. Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	Here is the translation:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The health of the two groins helps with the straightening of the ankle, and at the beginning of massage, and for many illnesses, and for pustules, and for corroding, and for herpes, and it is suitable; and the quality of the health is that the patients stretch their neck on one side and the other, as we have said; and so the masters standing above the patient's head, and the patient sits on a seat, then healthy vein of a length somewhat broadly, then draws out blood moderately, as much as necessary; then do another part in the other vein, then disentangle the ligament, and hold both veins moderately, so the patients are not strangled; and leave it until morning, so the wound is healthy.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins above the liver helps with pain in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips, and bad breath and inward.

de la sainie desoz la lengue	about the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are beneath the tongue helps after the health of the head, and it's about the constriction of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healthy one is that the patient places themselves between your hands before the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks beneath on each side a black vein: heal then one and the other, and do not go too deeply, for beneath are the arteries.

The veins of the neck that one commonly heals are healthy in two ways: either by pricking into the entire flame strongly, or by subtly feeling with a subtle touch as you feel the pulse, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame mirror is very renowned, and it is large as you see:

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids the illnesses that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it behooves the healer to bleed strongly, and to beware of the artery that is beneath.

And if you want to examine the joint of the vein, then it is necessary that you stretch out the arm, so that you touch the joint as much as you recognize the pulse; then mark the joint with an inch, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein at a gentle flame; and beware not to strike into the artery when you see the joint swollen, for it is of the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it swelling upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is not of the artery: hurry then, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops; bind the arm, and let it be, and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move until they are healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stagnant, and it flows well, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery so it opens, for the head of the veins retreats; and stagnates the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a poultice of fistula, and apply it, and take one of the medicines and lay it on well just next to the other day; if the wound is stagnant, that's good; if not, then cure, as we have said, with powders that staunch blood; and the staunching is not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the possibility of a strong liaison of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The health of the vein is in a thousand ways if it helps to draw blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the healer to be aware of the nerve that is below, and if he presses too hard, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the health becomes grievous, and by chance cannot be healed; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any homes due to its subtlety, then it is necessary that you anoint the instrument with oil; and chase away the nerve at your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two fingers, then they make it two inches long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The sanity of the head is helped when it attracts blood from the chief vein and helps the eyes; and one must help by pricking in the vein of olive oil or in the vein of myrtle, for it is the safest of all veins, since it has neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Always, one must seek the lightest vein, and not grievously harm oneself on the first attempt, and start again; and by chance, one inflames the veins in some men, although it happens on the first attempt, but it does not grievously harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is not administered for the sake of causing harm, but to preserve health and to prevent diseases to come; and so bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins that are on the arm: namely, cephalic, fastidial, and basilic; and one must bleed at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating, when signs of repletion appear; and one must bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The wisdom that is ministered to the sick has no hour determined, but only when need is by day or night, in all hours and in all tensions; and it does not suit to heal children up to 13 years, nor a woman carrying fruit for less than seven months until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One should not consider as healthy those who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to heal, in whatever manner it may be, one must first purify the intestines with a light clistere, if they have much flatulence retained, so that the veins do not attract superfluous and harmful humors to the principal members; nor does one heal those who are too full of meats, or drunkards, as long as it may be, nor dropsical people; and beware of healing after colic passion, and vomiting, and stomach decay, and multiple childbearing in women, and labor, and watching, and fasting, and all such virtues, or by means of the arm or whole body; then subtle humors, if the blood is gross, through meats and drinks and medicines, if you have much power; then take a bath, so that nothing defies, to subtly purify the blood, and heal the vein from the third vein, as we have said; and guard against that day of labor, and pain, and luxury, and similar things; and be gentle and joyful, and let the healer be more elevated than those who are healed, and rub the arm II times or III, then stretch out the lien moderately, because when it is too stretched or short, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the hand as much, until the veins swell, and feel them; then anoint the healer with a little oil of old wine, then put their left hand on the vein under the hand a little while they want to heal, so that the vein does not flee or fail to strike.

Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthy in the place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf. Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bloodletting of the little finger of the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is the method: hold the hand, and put it in warm water, until the vein becomes swollen, so that you can see it; and if the blood flows through the passage, and if you take it from everywhere, do not grieve anything; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are almost bare of skin, and then put the hand back in warm water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot get out.

Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The treatment of the spine is effective for all the diseases that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the liver, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.

And the quality of its treatment is that the patient feels pain in hot and cold water, and rubs against the vein until it perspires, and lays above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot many veins go to the rains; therefore, the treatment is given where the vein is larger, or at the ankle, which is more valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you apply it to the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and the vein that runs across like a bow; and let the flames be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the sans (sinew or tendon) cannot come out, put the foot in water, and let the vein be well cleansed.

Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein for sciatic pain is at the seat of fire, and its health is worth the pain in the thigh, when it is due to bad blood.

des sainies de ventouse	the healthiness of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping is made of horns, or of iron, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by pricking and attracting blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is without piercing if it is according to two methods: either it is with fire, or without fire; and cupping that is done by piercing and by extraction of blood is done in 13 veins of the body, from which one is all in the head; and another is in the neck; and two others are in the sides of the neck; and the cupping under the chin; and the cupping on the shoulders; and the cupping on the hips; and the cuppings on the arms; and the cuppings on the legs; and the cuppings on the ankles; and the cupping does not draw any blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason one should not be afraid of it, as one does with health of a vein; and it is not necessary that it be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illnesses it is necessary to evacuate, either by habit or custom, if we delay each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every season; for there are those who, when they have mastery over evacuating, have a heavy head; and if there are those who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and taste blood; and if there are those who sigh, and see by night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command to bleed them after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The health of the nose helps with the greatness of the head … which comes into the eyes, and it is not suitable that it be after the evacuation of all the body; and this evacuation is in the place of the health of the cephalic, and it is not suitable for those who are of cold complexion or have catarrh, because they make great harm to themselves; and therefore it is not suitable for the weak to use it, nor for those who have colds or evil diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often sane, if they become oblivious, and therefore it is suitable to put the cupping glass a little further down due to the doubt of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is in the place of the healthy head and the basilica, and for this reason it has strength in the extension of the chest, and in the splitting of the channel of the arm, and in touch, and in repletion; and it must hardly be touched, because if it holds too firmly, it injures the oblique or stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilations as the ribs of the neck have strength against the pains of the head, and obtundity and migraine, and in strangulation, and in pain as roots of the teeth, and are in the place of the healthiness of the basilica; and it is necessary that you instruct the healthy one to put their hand, so they do not touch the artery, and do not show signs of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The bad breath that comes from the mouth is a sign of disease in the mouth, and of gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the veins of the gums.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The bad breath from the palate indicates a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilations of the joints have strength as much as the three veins of the arm, because they attract blood from these large veins; and instruct the healthy one to not make too many movements in the font, because the joint is nude of flesh, and knows of nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping that is on the back is useful for removing excess from the foundation, and for illnesses beneath, and it is necessary that the cupping be large, and be of a good quality, so it can treat well; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cuppings of the legs are useful apparently, because they attract blood from the whole body, and alleviate ancient pains in the kidneys, and in the marrow, and in the bladder, and restore the flow; and they are in the place of .ij. sophenes, and of .ij. chevilles, and altogether they refresh the body after long use, and bring forth pus in more favorable dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping is that you put it on first void, and suck immediately, and place hastily, and remove evenly, and do not cease from doing this, until you see the red and inflamed spot, and appear the rosy color of blood; then firm, and reapply the cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have tender skin, and clear pores: if it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deeper; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is abundant, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to subtly open the way for the abundant blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike three times; and when we want to draw out a little blood at a time, then we suffice with striking only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to remove much blood, we often recommend it; and if the blood is thick, we make a fontanel, and the ends are so that the coursing is perceived suddenly, and it is necessary for one who has coarse skin and hard, and who have stiff pores, that you open the veins of oil apertif and dissolutif: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or of almond oil sweet, or of cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of cress oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is thick and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or oil of aniseed, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if it is for one who has tender skin and large pores, it does not need oil, but rather washing after the vein opening with rose water, or cold water, or water of morelle, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, if it rises from the ashes, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have gross superfluities lift themselves with wine vinegar, or water of elder, or decoction of anet or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not fitting to apply a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and one should not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that he warms himself when he must be cupped and when he is being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who are healthy and choleric, and their blood is too agitated and inflamed; if it is necessary that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in the shade, and similar things; and eat few pucins, and flesh of pike, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat few pucins and small birds and pigeons; and on the day they are to be cupped, they should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some people three or four times a draught of triacle or muscat before the cupping, or after, to comfort the principal members; and let the blood be subtle, but it is not fitting that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Here is the translation:
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of administration of fire cautery is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And have two inches and a half of palm in front, and have the edge cut into the middle of the small perforation, just as if to put a needle, and be of iron, soft in front so that it does not bother the patient when putting it on the limb; and have in the middle a crossbeam of iron or steel, to put a bandage in place, and they are large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the bandages of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin than the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should put this bandage on the limb: take the wax or lime thread, and put it in the bandage across the crossbeam which is in the bandage, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the bandage lest it burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and these two are on the small perforation as we have said, so that when one wants to remove it, the vapor goes out, and one removes the bandage; and take the thread as before, and often reapply it, if you have mastery.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the application of cupping when it is administered in disease of the lungs, at every ague, there is no vein nor perforation, and it is not administered except when it is full of ague, and is placed on the limb only slightly; and that is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without veins, they are not administered except in members where you cannot put cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and jaws, and similar places; and in the naked skin of flesh, such as fingers or toes, and similar things; and the quality of the use is that when you find without veins that are in soft, gentle, and smooth skin without porosity, take them; and put a nut in a soft and gentle cup, so they become familiar, and have nothing in the way of veins; and then be healthy with vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and put on the without veins; and when they will be full, and desire, it is the place where you can put a cupping glass, so put it, for that is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	Here is the translation:
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the sinews do not want to take, then rub the vein of fresh blood, or you fix a needle as long as the sinew is in it, and then set them up, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will be strengthened; and when you see that they cling, sprinkle a little powder of alum and of crushed brooknute, or of cinder, so they will hold now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This cautery is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a restoration of breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish mirrors themselves of this chapter, which they did not see in any of the ancient books, nor did they read a letter; and for this reason is the science strange in our land, because I did not find any good in it; and I do not know anything, except through the science of the ancient books, where I have so studied that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habituation of my life; and I have described to you here in this chapter what is contained, and I have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise men put their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when breakage or dislocation or twisting or bruising occurs to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from one part and another, so nothing harms them completely, as from weakness of body, or faintness, or old age; or if their tension is not very strong, or too cold; and moderate cold foods, these are to know frozen juices, and flesh of capon and goat, and do not drink any wine, and do not eat many greasy meats that fill the veins with blood, so you have no fear of hot abscess, nor expansion of matter in the limb; if the patient returns to their first governance which they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.
